 Dependency analysis for extraction order:

**responsive.ts dependencies:**
- Vue: ref, computed, watch, toValue, Ref, ComputedRef
- VueUse: useMounted (passed in)
- Target element (passed in)
- Responsive options interface
- NO dependencies on other extracted modules

**svg.ts dependencies:**
- Vue: computed, toValue, ComputedRef, CSSProperties
- Target element (passed in)
- SVG options interface
- NO dependencies on other extracted modules

**grid.ts dependencies:**
- Vue: computed, toValue, ComputedRef, CSSProperties
- Target element (passed in)
- Grid options interface
- NO dependencies on other extracted modules

**enterExit.ts dependencies:**
- Vue: watch, ref, unref, Ref
- VueUse: useMounted (passed in)
- CRITICAL: Imports animationPresets from ./presets
- Uses ANIMATION_DURATION, EASING, FILL_MODE from constants
- Target element (passed in)
- EnterExit options interface

Extraction order: responsive, svg, grid can be parallel. enterExit depends on presets.ts (already extracted in Phase 1), so it's safe to extract last.

 Type extraction strategy for Phase 2. Need to identify all interfaces/types used by the 4 modules:

**responsive.ts types:**
- ResponsiveDimensions interface (width, height, scale, aspectRatio)
- UseAnimationResponsiveOptions (already exists in main file)
- ResponsiveSystem return type

**svg.ts types:**
- UseAnimationSvgOptions (viewBox, anchors)
- SvgSystem return type

**grid.ts types:**
- UseAnimationGridOptions (columns, rows, gap, zones)
- GridSystem return type

**enterExit.ts types:**
- UseAnimationEnterExitOptions (already exists in main file, lines 172-181)
- EnterExitOptions for setup function

Strategy: Move interface definitions to types.ts, keep function signatures in module files. This prevents circular imports and centralizes shared types.

  Thought 9/20 

 Coordination pattern for Phase 2 (Pattern 2 from plan: Cleanup Function Returns):

**In main file (index.ts):**
```typescript
// Setup phase (conditional)
let responsiveSystem = undefined
let cleanupResponsive = undefined
if (responsive) {
  const result = setupResponsive(target, isMounted, responsiveOptions)
  responsiveSystem = result.system
  cleanupResponsive = result.cleanup
}

// Similar for svg, grid, enterExit

// Return API includes systems
return {
  ...
  responsive: responsiveSystem,
  svg: svgSystem,
  grid: gridSystem,
  // enterExit doesn't expose system, just runs automatically
}

// Cleanup calls all cleanup functions in order
cleanup() {
  cleanupResponsive?.()
  cleanupSvg?.() // if svg has cleanup
  cleanupGrid?.() // if grid has cleanup
  cleanupEnterExit?.()
}
```

This maintains single entry point, preserves cleanup order, allows conditional feature usage.

 Validation strategy per extraction (from plan):

**For each module (responsive, svg, grid, enterExit):**

1. **Unit validation** - Test module in isolation
   - responsive: ResizeObserver attaches/detaches, dimensions update, scale calculations
   - svg: Coordinate conversions accurate, anchor positioning correct
   - grid: Zone queries work, center calculations correct
   - enterExit: Trigger transitions work, animations play, callbacks fire

2. **Integration validation** - Test with main composable
   - Import works, no circular dependencies
   - Setup function called conditionally
   - System returned correctly in API
   - Cleanup called in correct order

3. **TypeScript validation** - Run tsc --noEmit
   - No type errors
   - Interfaces properly exported/imported
   - Generic types preserved

4. **Manual testing** - Check existing consumers
   - All 25+ consumer components still work
   - No runtime errors
   - Behavior unchanged

After all Phase 2 extractions: Run full test suite, check bundle size, verify performance.

 Detailed task breakdown for responsive.ts creation:

**File: useAnimation/responsive.ts**
1. Export ResponsiveDimensions, UseAnimationResponsiveOptions interfaces
2. Export setupResponsive function signature:
   - Parameters: target (MaybeRefOrGetter), isMounted (Ref<boolean>), options (UseAnimationResponsiveOptions)
   - Returns: { system: ResponsiveSystem, cleanup: () => void }
3. Inside setupResponsive:
   - Create dimensions ref<ResponsiveDimensions>
   - Create ResizeObserver with debounced updateDimensions
   - Setup watcher on [isMounted, target] to attach/detach observer
   - Create computed helpers: scaleValue, getResponsiveRadius, getResponsiveOffset, scaled
   - Return system object and cleanup function
4. Handle edge cases: ResizeObserver not supported, element missing, timing issues

Total lines: ~210 (including comments and error handling)

 Detailed task breakdown for svg.ts creation:

**File: useAnimation/svg.ts**
1. Export UseAnimationSvgOptions interface (viewBox, anchors)
2. Export setupSvg function signature:
   - Parameters: target (MaybeRefOrGetter), options (UseAnimationSvgOptions)
   - Returns: { system: SvgSystem } (no cleanup needed)
3. Inside setupSvg:
   - Create viewBoxString computed
   - Create svgScale computed (calculates x/y scale from element rect)
   - Create svgToScreen computed converter
   - Create screenToSvg computed converter
   - Create getAnchor function
   - Create anchorToStyle computed helper
   - Return system object
4. Pure computations, no side effects, no cleanup needed

Total lines: ~85 (including type safety and error handling)

 Risk assessment and mitigation for Phase 2:

**Risks:**
1. Circular imports - Mitigated by clear import hierarchy (presets  modules  index)
2. Type errors - Mitigated by proper interface exports and TypeScript validation
3. SSR safety - Mitigated by passing isMounted, checking before DOM access
4. Cleanup order - Mitigated by documented cleanup sequence
5. Breaking changes - Mitigated by maintaining return API structure

**Safety checks between each module:**
- Run `npm run typecheck` after each extraction
- Test import resolution
- Check no circular dependencies
- Manual test in at least one consumer component

**Rollback strategy:**
- Git commit after each successful module extraction
- If any module fails, revert that commit
- Phase 2 is independent from Phase 1, so can rollback Phase 2 entirely without affecting Phase 1

  Thought 18/20 

 Execution sequence optimization:

**Optimal order:**
1. Create responsive.ts first (largest, most complex, sets pattern)
2. Create svg.ts second (pure computations, simple)
3. Create grid.ts third (similar to svg, pure queries)
4. Create enterExit.ts fourth (depends on presets, has watchers)
5. Update index.ts once (all imports and setup calls together)
6. Run validation suite

**Why this order:**
- Responsive is most complex, establishes cleanup pattern
- Svg and grid are similar, can validate pattern consistency
- EnterExit is unique (watchers), benefits from seeing other patterns first
- Single index.ts update reduces merge conflicts and testing cycles

**Time estimates per module:**
- responsive.ts: 30 mins (complex with ResizeObserver)
- svg.ts: 15 mins (pure computations)
- grid.ts: 15 mins (similar to svg)
- enterExit.ts: 20 mins (watchers and callbacks)
- index.ts updates: 20 mins (careful removal and imports)
- Validation: 20 mins (typecheck, manual testing)
**Total: ~2 hours** (matches plan estimate of 2-3 hours)
